  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer13275973228621744417"><b>Imagine a place where the dead rest on shelves like books.</b><br/><br/>Each body has a story to tell, a life seen in pictures only Librarians can read. The dead are called Histories, and the vast realm in which they rest is the Archive.<br/><br/>Da first brought Mackenzie Bishop here four years ago, when she was twelve years old, frightened but determined to prove herself. Now Da is dead, and Ma</span>
  <span id="freeText13275973228621744417" style="display:none"><b>Imagine a place where the dead rest on shelves like books.</b><br /><br />Each body has a story to tell, a life seen in pictures only Librarians can read. The dead are called Histories, and the vast realm in which they rest is the Archive.<br /><br />Da first brought Mackenzie Bishop here four years ago, when she was twelve years old, frightened but determined to prove herself. Now Da is dead, and Mac has grown into what he once was: a ruthless Keeper, tasked with stopping often violent Histories from waking up and getting out. Because of her job, she lies to the people she loves, and she knows fear for what it is: a useful tool for staying alive.<br /><br />Being a Keeper isn't just dangerous—it's a constant reminder of those Mac has lost, Da's death was hard enough, but now that her little brother is gone too, Mac starts to wonder about the boundary between living and dying, sleeping and waking. In the Archive, the dead must never be disturbed. And yet, someone is deliberately altering Histories, erasing essential chapters. Unless Mac can piece together what remains, the Archive itself may crumble and fall.<br /><br />In this haunting, richly imagined novel, Victoria Schwab reveals the thin lines between past and present, love and pain, trust and deceit, unbearable loss and hard-won redemption.</span>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/734236-i-m-confused-is-her-dad-actually-dead">I&#39;m confused. Is her Dad actually dead? Cause she keeps referring to him like &#39;following him through the kitchen&#39; or whatever, but earlier she said he was dead. WHAT.</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_734236'><a id="like_count_community_question_734236" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/734236?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">5 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F10929432-the-archived">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/734236-i-m-confused-is-her-dad-actually-dead">4 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/734236-i-m-confused-is-her-dad-actually-dead">Add your answer</a>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/34935170-dhara-parekh"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1603147789i/34935170._UY100_CR26,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/34935170-dhara-parekh">Dhara Parekh</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
You are confusing "Dad" with "Da". She addresses her grandfather as Da, who is dead. Her dad is alive.
</span>

<div id="review_248182894" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/248182894" />
    <a title="Wendy Darling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling"><img alt="Wendy Darling" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379959930p2/2745288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/248182894?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy Darling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy Darling" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling">Wendy Darling</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=hyperion">hyperion</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=pn-ghosts">pn-ghosts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=2013-publication">2013-publication</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=january">january</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=read-2012">read-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=2013-favorites">2013-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=action-packed">action-packed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=sci-fi-or-futuristic">sci-fi-or-futuristic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=gorgeous-prose">gorgeous-prose</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer248182894" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2439194995453159188">I have to admit, it wasn't until the second half of the book that <i>The Archived</i> really started clicking together for me. I've heard that some people who read the extended preview online were unsure if they wanted to continue, and I can see why--but something about the writing was really appealing to me and I ended up having a great experience with it.<br/><br/><b>Here's what I liked about the book:</b><br/><br/>* Dead people who are kept on shelves like books? Sign me on! Awesome premise. <br/>* I loved the eerie, something's-n</span>
  <span id="freeText2439194995453159188" style="display:none">I have to admit, it wasn't until the second half of the book that <i>The Archived</i> really started clicking together for me. I've heard that some people who read the extended preview online were unsure if they wanted to continue, and I can see why--but something about the writing was really appealing to me and I ended up having a great experience with it.<br /><br /><b>Here's what I liked about the book:</b><br /><br />* Dead people who are kept on shelves like books? Sign me on! Awesome premise. <br />* I loved the eerie, something's-not-quite-right atmosphere. All this drama happening in the hushed hallways of a library setting somehow felt pretty creepy.<br />* The narrative voice felt comfortable and real.<br />* This isn't written in a fast-paced sci-fi thriller kind of way, and I liked the slower pace and somewhat contemplative tone.<br />* The part of the story involving mysterious murders in an old hotel-turned-apartment-building was intriguing, and the way the clues gradually reveal themselves is enjoyable.<br />* I really liked some of the characters, especially the stern Roland, an older Librarian who mentors Mackenzie.<br /><br /><b>Things that were just fine:</b><br /><br />* The romantic interests. Yes, there is an "s" at the end of that, but there isn't really a love triangle here, and things are just interesting enough without overtaking the entire plot.<br />* The villain. Maybe a bit too easy to guess, but not until closer to the end.<br /><br /><b>Things I felt could use improvement:</b><br /><br />* I found the beginning very confusing, in part because I thought "Da" referred to Mackenzie's father, not her grandfather. The timeline also moved back and forth too much for my taste, and the switches in tense itched at me. Also, does her brother's death have some further significance at some point? Between that, her grandfather's death, moving to a new home, etc., there was a lot to take in the opening chapters.<br /><br />* I was also never entirely sure how I understood how the mechanics of everything works in the Library or the Keepers' exact roles. There were also definitely parts where I thought, "No way!" or "I don't get why this just didn't happen."<br /><br />But there came a point when the story started coming together and taking off that I just let go of my doubts and just enjoyed the ride. In fact, I think zoomed through the last half in one sitting, it was such a page-turner! The book is well-plotted, well-written, and touched with some darkness, as well as humor. This isn't a typical sci-fi story, and it's all the better for that. I'm tired of wham-bam adventure stories that do little more than connect the dots between one action scene to the next.<br /><br />This is the first book I've read by this author, but given the many positive reviews I've seen for her debut, I think I need to seek out <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6931344.The_Near_Witch__The_Near_Witch___1_" title="The Near Witch (The Near Witch, #1) by Victoria Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">The Near Witch</a> very soon. And of course, I'll be waiting for the new batch of Archives in the coming year.<br /><br /><i>This review also appears in <a href="http://www.themidnightgarden.net/2013/01/the-archived-review-giveaway.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Midnight Garden</a>. An advance copy was provided by the publisher.</i><br /><br />You can also <a href="http://www.themidnightgarden.net/2013/01/the-archived-review-giveaway.html" rel="nofollow noopener">win an ARC of The Archived</a> on the blog! </span>
  <a data-text-id="2439194995453159188" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_497851576" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/497851576" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/497851576?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer497851576" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5821545055846511641"><b>Oh yes hello, I think I am thoroughly doomed to adore everything written by Schwab.</b> <i>Everything</i> omg. This book was incredible. It's so unique and the writing just hit me and the characters were all tortured and adorable and somewhat sassy -- AND QUITE FOND OF BAKED GOODS -- so basically I am Schwab trash and not even sad about it.<br/><br/>Also I hear the 3rd book is like...never ever coming out??? SLAY ME. (I ordered the sequel though, so let me read that, and <i>then</i> slay me.)<br/><br/><b>What really REALLY hit me (omg </b></span>
  <span id="freeText5821545055846511641" style="display:none"><b>Oh yes hello, I think I am thoroughly doomed to adore everything written by Schwab.</b> <i>Everything</i> omg. This book was incredible. It's so unique and the writing just hit me and the characters were all tortured and adorable and somewhat sassy -- AND QUITE FOND OF BAKED GOODS -- so basically I am Schwab trash and not even sad about it.<br /><br />Also I hear the 3rd book is like...never ever coming out??? SLAY ME. (I ordered the sequel though, so let me read that, and <i>then</i> slay me.)<br /><br /><b>What really REALLY hit me (omg violent little book) was how unique the story was!</b> It's like a library but for DEAD PEOPLE. And sometimes the dead people escape and wonder around these dark hallways (kind of like purgatory I guess?) and they must have Keepers to haul 'em back to deadness. <b>Meet Keeper = Mackenzie Bishop.</b> She's such a tortured soul and I totally liked her. But you know what I liked even more? THE MAGICNESS AND THE LIBRARY AND THE DEAD PEOPLE. It was all creepy and vaguely dark and I could totally see it as a Tim Burton movie playing out in my head. A+++ basically. <br /><br /><b>And the characters?! Precious little mites.</b> Like I said: TORTURED. When you're a Keeper your life is like <b>(A) </b>lying to everyone because they can't know about your Other Life Chasing Dead People Back To Their Shelves, and<b> (B)</b> you get memories from things you touch, so no touchee to anyone, which makes things lonely, and <b>(C)</b> apparently you have an automatic ginormous need for baked goods. Loving it.<br /><br />So apart from Mackenzie (who narrates in 1st person), she meets <b>Wes</b> who is a smooth-talking and slightly goth dude who got a book thrown at his head, <i>caught it</i>, and carried on a conversation about muffins at the same time. I'm 10000% a gonner and in love. <b>And later on Mackenzie meets Owen in the purgatory-sort-of-place and he is equally mystery and tortured.</b> SO I AM A FAN.<br /><br />Um...<b>I suppose you could say there's a love triangle??</b> But it doesn't <i>feel</i> like one because Mackenzie is suffering from SERIOUS GRIEF over the death of her brother and she's not in the kissing mood. #thankgoodness So there are 2 boys. There are attractions. There are plot twists (HUGE!! PLOT!! TWISTS!!) involving both boys. (And I also love both boys. So there you go.) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Although I did think Owen and Mac's pashing came out of nowhere. I mean, he was dead, so we know that ship wasn't sailing.... also I was immensely pleased Owen turned out to be evil. I LOVE OWEN. I SHOULD PROBABLY BE CONCERNED BUT I'M NOT. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>I suppose you could say everything is just glorious.</b> It just ticked sooooo many boxes for me. Mackenzie was withdrawn, but not emotionless and she was easy to connect to. And the world took me a little while to get the hang of, but THEN I WAS THERE and it was <i>so so vivid</i>. Plus I just love the idea of a library of dead people. Seriously. Love. This is amazing. Why did I not read this earlier? (Spoiler: because I'm an idiot.)<br /><br />Althoooough I maintain the BEST Schwab books are <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22055262.A_Darker_Shade_of_Magic__Shades_of_Magic___1_" title="A Darker Shade of Magic (Shades of Magic, #1) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">A Darker Shade of Magic</a> series. <br /><br /><b>You probably definitely completely need this one in your life.</b> I have so many questions I AM DYING FOR THE SEQUEL. And I just loved being emerged in Schwab's style of writing again. I adored the plot twists! The aesthetics! The humour!! AND DEFINITELY THE FOOD. (It was partially set in a cafe omg.) I'm just going t leave this quote here and be happy:<br />"Hey," he says, knocking his shoe playfully against mine. "It's the same for me, you know? This is all new to me. And I'm not going anywhere. It takes at least three assassination attempts to scare me off. And even then, if there are baked goods involved, I might come back."</span>
  <a data-text-id="5821545055846511641" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1130869550?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Cristina Monica by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/14811808-liz">Liz</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=originality">originality</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1130869550" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16824309840168294052"> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418503231i/12812186.jpg' width='400' height='230' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Thinking back, I don’t remember ever reading something quite like this story before. It was very creative and imaginative, I have to say. The concept refreshing and interesting to read about. Although, there were many things that didn’t work for me as well as they did for multiple other book lovers who read this mysterious looking book. <br/><br/>For being mysterious, that it sure was, especially at the beginning. I was eager to learn everything about the main character’s ability and the world-building, </span>
  <span id="freeText16824309840168294052" style="display:none"> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418503231i/12812186.jpg" width="400" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Thinking back, I don’t remember ever reading something quite like this story before. It was very creative and imaginative, I have to say. The concept refreshing and interesting to read about. Although, there were many things that didn’t work for me as well as they did for multiple other book lovers who read this mysterious looking book. <br><br>For being mysterious, that it sure was, especially at the beginning. I was eager to learn everything about the main character’s ability and the world-building, needless to say. As the story slowly unfolded itself though, I realized that what was under its white silky fabric (feeling the ghostly atmosphere yet?) was not as impressive as I first predicted…but it had great constituents still.<br><br>I’ve thought about it…and the protagonist was too young for me. I like my MCs to be <i>at least</i> sixteen years old in my reads. It’s just a personal preference I have, because I like my heroines’ age to be as close to mine as possible so there could be a better possibility of connection.<br><br>Mac is a Keeper. She keeps Histories. Histories are like…data collections of dead people but, in their own form. That’s how I see them, but they truly aren’t completely explained in the book, if not at the beginning only in brief descriptions. Except an image can easily be made of them after reading this. So each ‘History’ is to be resting in the Achieve, the library – as you can call it – after their death. However, sometimes, a History or two can escape…and Mac’s job is to find them and put them back where they belong. It may seem simple, but it’s not. Especially not when stumbling upon a circumstance of events you do not understand. Someone killed a History, in Mac’s own room, and she needs to find who did it.<br><br>Even if the pacing starts off pretty slow, the story does pick up and upgrades its speed to a most engaging one as chapters go by. The writing is also pleasant and I believe suiting the story and main character’s voice best. Not the secondary ones. See, most of the secondary characters, except for Mac’s dead brothers, Wesley, Roland and the Histories she is strongly helping, feel one-dimensional. I guess it can be because the heroine didn’t give much importance to many. Even the parents…they’re uninteresting and unfortunately boring and forgettable.<br><br>The love interest (&lt;-- what a twist!) was really well-developed. I thought the author brought a very pertinent element to the story by including that character. What I liked most was that it wasn’t a romance novel alone and that the romance itself doesn’t steal some importance anywhere. And, by the way, Wesley, Mac’s ‘friend’ reminded me of Jace from <b>The Mortal Instruments</b>, with his personality. He was the most entertaining of them all.<br><br>What I really didn’t like about the main character though was how easily and often she lied. She did it in every chapter at least two times and it became annoying after some time. Even if she might have felt bad after, it doesn’t change that she didn’t find any other solution than to do that. When a character actually has says: <i>
  <b>‘‘It’s the only thing I’ve said that wasn’t a lie,’’</b>
</i> then there is a problem. Her choice of concealing the truth was understandable, depending on the scene, but the so many lies started to frustrate me because, see, the people she lied to didn’t necessarily deserve it.<br><br>Also, in the story, the narrator didn’t describe the Histories as ghosts, yet, that’s how they appeared to me. The way they talked, moved and just overall; it gave me as impression that they were indeed ghosts…when I don’t think this was the author’s wish. But that wasn’t a negative point, since it didn’t bother me at all.<br><br>Overall, it was intriguing and enjoyable enough. I hope less lies will be present in the sequel, because I do intend to read it sometime soon. The world-building has a lot of potential, being different from what we’re used to, but the settings could use some variety. The romance was, even if of small importance, lovely, but it could have used more romantic scenes to make it more believable…yet I do understand why the author did not include more. Nonetheless, this was a good book with twists and turns that were remarkable and honestly unpredictable! <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="16824309840168294052" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1426426904" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1426426904" />
    <a title="Simona B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b"><img alt="Simona B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408893128p2/5312173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1426426904?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781423171089" href="/book/show/17899647-the-archived">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=fantastic-lit-and-co">fantastic-lit-and-co</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1426426904" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3910162398178381246"><b>"Curiosity is a gateway drug to sympathy."</b><br/><br/>•Do you know when you start a book with preconceptions and you somehow end up liking/not liking the book <i>exactly</i> in the degree you knew you would? Well, I started this book with preconceptions. I liked just as much as I thought I would. That is,<b> a lot</b>.<br/><br/>•Since I am fairly sure you grew tired of my eulogies of <b>Schwab's writing</b> a long time ago, I redirect you to my reviews of <i><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1305000667?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Darker Shade of Magic</a>,</i> <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1559469393?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Gathering of Shadows</a>
</i> and <i><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1437808191?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>This Savage Song</a>.</i> Generally</span>
  <span id="freeText3910162398178381246" style="display:none"><b>"Curiosity is a gateway drug to sympathy."</b><br /><br />•Do you know when you start a book with preconceptions and you somehow end up liking/not liking the book <i>exactly</i> in the degree you knew you would? Well, I started this book with preconceptions. I liked just as much as I thought I would. That is,<b> a lot</b>.<br /><br />•Since I am fairly sure you grew tired of my eulogies of <b>Schwab's writing</b> a long time ago, I redirect you to my reviews of <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1305000667?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">A Darker Shade of Magic</a>,</i> <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1559469393?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">A Gathering of Shadows</a>
</i> and <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1437808191?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">This Savage Song</a>.</i> Generally speaking, I found the writing in <i>The Archived</i> <b>slightly less brilliant </b>than what I came to think of as Schwab's usual, but not once was I really unhappy with it. Knowing how picky and hard to please I normally am, my constant and unshakable satisfaction with what comes out of this author's mind is probably the closest thing to a miracle I've ever seen or heard of in my life.<br /><br />•Of course, <b>each one of Schwab's books has something that makes it absolutely unique</b>. The Shades of Magic trilogy has, needless to say, magic; <i>Vicious</i> has superpowers and anthiheroes; The Monsters of Verity series has monsters. One would say <i>The Archived</i> has a library of the dead, and that that is more than enough to make it unforgettable, and that would be true, but not quite, because actually the thing about <i>The Archived</i> that will leave a permament mark on your heart is its <b>grief</b>. The grief of its characters, of its pages, of its story; the book is so soaked in it that it itself seems to be mourning. It's <b>beautiful and sad</b>, and so simply, gracefully rendered. The <b>sense of loss that permeates every page</b> is, to me, the reason why this story will stand out forever from the infinity of other stories I've read or heard. <br /><br />•I had gotten use to Schwab's characters to be a little reserved, maybe kind of <b>standoffish</b>, and when I read <i>Our Savage Song</i> I was pleasantly surprised to make the acquaintance of two protagonists who seemed to be so vulnerable. Well, <b>Mackenzie Bishop</b> and <b>Wesley Ayers</b> are more <b>open </b>and unguarded yet. They are strong, they are fighters, but their weaknesses and their <b>loneliness</b> are <b>a blow to the heart</b>. They made me pshysically ache inside. It is impossible not to connect with characters -no, with <i>people</i>- like them. <br /><br />➽ As I stated elsewere, <b>its' Schwab's, it's good</b>. My favourite remains <i>A Darker Shade of Magic</i>, but <i>The Archived</i> has its peculiar charms. I still have to read the second book and I'm already terrified because it's not sure we'll have the third. <br />I need another miracle.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3910162398178381246" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1243878006" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1243878006" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1243878006?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1243878006" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14567760837150918608"><i>“Because the only way to truly record a person is not in words, not in still frames, but in bone and skin and memory.”</i><br/><br/>This was stunning.<br/>I loved the beginning, the language, the setting and the whole concept. Victoria Schwab can do some real magic with words, which is why I loved this book even more. She is one of the most talented voices in fantasy/YA/science fiction literature and I am baffled and amazed by her writing. <i>The Archived </i> is such a beautiful collection of words. I can't get enough.<br/><br/>I</span>
  <span id="freeText14567760837150918608" style="display:none"><i>“Because the only way to truly record a person is not in words, not in still frames, but in bone and skin and memory.”</i><br /><br />This was stunning.<br />I loved the beginning, the language, the setting and the whole concept. Victoria Schwab can do some real magic with words, which is why I loved this book even more. She is one of the most talented voices in fantasy/YA/science fiction literature and I am baffled and amazed by her writing. <i>The Archived </i> is such a beautiful collection of words. I can't get enough.<br /><br />I love mysteries, but the sad truth is that once solved they are less interesting and, well...less mysterious. I often find that I expected more and I'm therefore a little disappointed with the outcome. That's what happened here. (Which doesn't keep it from being a great book)<br />I have to admit that I really fell for some of the characters. Da, Wesley, Ben and some other minor ones. Everybody and everything just seemed so real.<br /><br />Please. Write faster and give me more magic, Victoria.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14567760837150918608" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_327298452" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/327298452" />
    <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair"><img alt="Steph Sinclair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457555690p2/4642710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/327298452?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Sinclair" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair">Steph Sinclair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Anna Dressed in Blood and murder mysteries </span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2013-release">2013-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=oh-yeah-baby">oh-yeah-baby</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=disney-hyperion">disney-hyperion</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=surprised-me">surprised-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=gave-away">gave-away</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2013-favorite">2013-favorite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=best-characters">best-characters</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer327298452" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7267717993272784886">Actual rating: 4.5<br/><br/>I truly underestimated this book. You know how when you first read a book's blurb and it totally catches your attention as something different and unique? You know that feeling right afterwards that can only be described nothing short of "Gimme Syndrome"? Yeah, that's how I felt with <em>The Archived.</em> But for whatever reason, I got distracted and started picking up other books (you know how it is). Well, one day I was frolicking through my bookshelf, re-read the blurb and engaged t</span>
  <span id="freeText7267717993272784886" style="display:none">Actual rating: 4.5<br><br>I truly underestimated this book. You know how when you first read a book's blurb and it totally catches your attention as something different and unique? You know that feeling right afterwards that can only be described nothing short of "Gimme Syndrome"? Yeah, that's how I felt with <em>The Archived.</em> But for whatever reason, I got distracted and started picking up other books (you know how it is). Well, one day I was frolicking through my bookshelf, re-read the blurb and engaged the family in a battle of epic proportions for peace and quiet.<br><br><img alt="Jedi-kitten battle" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380377392i/732677.jpg" width="400" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><em>I won. Obviously.</em><br><br>It was a good thing that I had managed to find this rare thing called reading time, because once I started reading <em>The Archived,</em> I didn't want to stop. Oh boy, Schwab. I am a fan! The premise is so fascinating and fleshed out in the book, that you can't help but to drink the descriptions in. Just imagine a library existing for people who die with the sole purpose of preserving their memories. Then you'd have these Librarians who would catalogue the dead and Keepers to Return the Histories (the dead) to the Archive (library). Like I said, truly fascinating and I think Schawb really pulled it off well.<br><br>Mac was a fantastic main character. She was smart, resourceful and very relatable. In the beginning, we learn that she has lost both her grandfather, who she refers to as "Da", and her younger brother. The pain and grief that she feels for her brother, in particular, felt very realistic to me. There were scenes where she was desperate to hold onto her brother's memory by clinging to items that once belonged to him. Her feelings of guilt for not being able to protect him, anger at her parents for attempting to move on, frustration at herself for not remembering every detail about him, all resonated with me quite a bit due to my own personal experiences. I thought Mac was brave for dealing with her grief while still upholding her Keeper duties and coming in contact with Histories everyday.<br><br>Speaking of Histories, I thought that was a really creative way to show a new kind of paranormal character. I would almost classify them as a ghost/zombie hybrid. They look exactly like their human selves except for their eyes. They talk, walk around in corporeal forms and are generally confused about their whereabouts. They also don't know they are dead. (Yikes! Talk about being the bearer of bad news...) Because of that little complication, Mac has to sometimes fight the Histories, forcing them back to the Returns. If you are having trouble with picturing that scenario, just think of Cas hunting ghosts from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9378297-anna-dressed-in-blood" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Anna Dressed in Blood</em>
</a> and you'll have a pretty good idea.<br><br>The plot is where a lot of the magic in <em>The Archived</em> happens. Schwab really wove a great mystery together that had me flipping pages without letup. Since she created a world so different from what I usually seen in YA lit, I was completely surprised at the twists and turns. The ending to this murder mystery is something I never saw coming.<br><br>Oh and *high fives Schwab for the love interest* I LOVED Wes. Even though he didn't get a ton of page time, I enjoyed the refreshing comical flare he brought to the story. I especially love how his existence didn't take over Mac's life. 'Cause the girl had bigger fish to fry, like, say hunting Histories, making sure they didn't escape into the real world and murder people in their sleep. Kinda important.<br><br>The only reason why I'm not giving out 5 stars is due to the beginning. It was a little slow and complex with the narrative mode switching back and forth. Sometimes Mac is narrating to the audience and other times she's chronicling her past Keeper lessons with her grandfather, but it's like she's narrating to him (ex. "We used to do this or that together, Da.") I adjusted to this style pretty quickly, but I can see it throwing off other readers a bit. However, hang in there because the flip-flopping tapers off pretty quickly as the story progresses. Not to mention the second half is simply phenomenal.<br><br>Anyway, brilliant, brilliant, brilliant. I definitely highly recommend people check out <em>The Archived.</em> It's the perfect murder mystery to keep you on the edge of your seat. It's the kind of book that had me thinking about the events long after I finished and now I'll be desperately waiting for book 2.<br><br><em>ARC was received from the publisher. Thanks, Disney-Hyperion!</em><br><br>More reviews and other fantastical things at <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery Book Blog</a>. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7267717993272784886" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1712575449" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1712575449" />
    <a title="sreeja" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50309540-sreeja"><img alt="sreeja" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598363186p2/50309540.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1712575449?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="sreeja" class="user" itemprop="url" name="sreeja" href="/user/show/50309540-sreeja">sreeja</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50309540-sreeja?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50309540-sreeja?shelf=fantasy-reads">fantasy-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1712575449" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15590399721081276950"> <b>
  <i>“Ignorance may be bliss, but only if it outweighs curiosity. Curiosity is a gateway drug to sympathy.”</i>
</b><br/>The Archived: 4.25 stars <br/><i> Reasons why reading it was worth it:</i><br/>•Victoria Schwab’s writing (so amazing <3)<br/>•Wesley Ayers<br/>•Wesley Ayers<br/>•Wesley Ayers<br/><br/><a href='http://s1064.photobucket.com/user/simplysreeja/media/adore_zps5crn3hpm.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478767023ra/21108819.gif' alt=' photo adore_zps5crn3hpm.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/> <b>yes somehow guyliner managed to squeeze and find a place in my heart</b><br/><br/>The Archived is a book that you learn to love more and more as time goes on. The beautiful descriptions and the spot on characters with flaws who get real time consequences for </span>
  <span id="freeText15590399721081276950" style="display:none"> <b>
  <i>“Ignorance may be bliss, but only if it outweighs curiosity. Curiosity is a gateway drug to sympathy.”</i>
</b><br>The Archived: 4.25 stars <br><i> Reasons why reading it was worth it:</i><br>•Victoria Schwab’s writing (so amazing &lt;3)<br>•Wesley Ayers<br>•Wesley Ayers<br>•Wesley Ayers<br><br><a href="http://s1064.photobucket.com/user/simplysreeja/media/adore_zps5crn3hpm.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478767023ra/21108819.gif" alt=" photo adore_zps5crn3hpm.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br> <b>yes somehow guyliner managed to squeeze and find a place in my heart</b><br><br>The Archived is a book that you learn to love more and more as time goes on. The beautiful descriptions and the spot on characters with flaws who get real time consequences for their actions. I never expected to like this book as much as I really did. I think with Victoria Schwab books I don’t feel pressured to read as fast as I can and instead I savour the way she writes and her descriptions of the places. Same with Vicious, I was in no hurry to finish it but once I reached the end I realised how much I loved it and how much the characters had grown on me. <br><br>The entire concept of this book was so unique and interesting that I definitely had to pick it up. I mean a place where the dead are kept as records of their human selves. How freaking cool is that. The options as to where this story could have gone was endless. However, the plot decided to focus on a mystery closer to the whereabouts of Mackenzie, our main protagonist. I wouldn’t say that I was a huge fan of her though. Main reason being her stupid decisions (sorry mac), but Da would definitely not have been a fan of what you did. I can understand where she was coming from when she made the decisions that he did but that does not mean that she actually should have ultimately made the choices that she did, after all the experience that she has and the training that she went through. But I guess in the end she is human and she was going through a lot.<br><a href="http://s1064.photobucket.com/user/simplysreeja/media/Harry-Potter-I-Dunno-Shrug-Reaction-Gif_zpsrexbzjj2.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478767023ra/21108820.gif" alt=" photo Harry-Potter-I-Dunno-Shrug-Reaction-Gif_zpsrexbzjj2.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>I am seriously becoming a huge fan of Victoria Schwab and the way she writes! There is something so magical and beautiful in her writing style that just draws you in I swear. I’m definitely more excited to pick up more books by her now.<br><br>The fantasy element in this book is so good and I felt connected even with the minor characters of this book! Seriously the neighbours that Mac had were absolutely hilarious HAHA. The hierarchy of the Archived and the way it works was kept in the dark from Mackenzie and it felt good to learn about these new things for the first time through her eyes. <br><br>Also this book was made so much better by the presence of Wesley Ayers! Their banter was adorable and I really wish we could have seen even more of him in this book because he was hilarious and supportive and super sweet. <br><br>Overall, this book was a blast and I’m sure the next one will be great as well but I might read it next year because I feel perfectly content with the way things ended off in this book. This book was very intriguing and Victoria Schwab’s writing just makes this book amazing!<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="15590399721081276950" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1009161734" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1009161734" />
    <a title="Nina (Every Word A Doorway)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32524334-nina-every-word-a-doorway"><img alt="Nina (Every Word A Doorway)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456070558p2/32524334.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1009161734?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nina (Every Word A Doorway)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nina (Every Word A Doorway)" href="/user/show/32524334-nina-every-word-a-doorway">Nina (Every Word A Doorway)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32524334-nina-every-word-a-doorway?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1009161734" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15865475012560810535"><b>My love for Victoria Schwab's books – and Wesley Ayers – knows no boundaries. This was so good.</b> Now, excuse me while I go do my happy dance because this was my first 4-star read this year, the short stories not included (which is sad, but glass half full, am I right?). <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1448298914ra/17119716.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Though published prior to her bestselling <em>Darker Shade of Magic </em>series, I picked up <em>The Archived</em> a lot later. It stands in the shadow of Schwab's more popular releases, and though it is far less hyped, <em>The Archived</em> has no reason t</span>
  <span id="freeText15865475012560810535" style="display:none"><b>My love for Victoria Schwab's books – and Wesley Ayers – knows no boundaries. This was so good.</b> Now, excuse me while I go do my happy dance because this was my first 4-star read this year, the short stories not included (which is sad, but glass half full, am I right?). <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1448298914ra/17119716.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Though published prior to her bestselling <em>Darker Shade of Magic </em>series, I picked up <em>The Archived</em> a lot later. It stands in the shadow of Schwab's more popular releases, and though it is far less hyped, <em>The Archived</em> has no reason to hide. <strong>The Archived is – as are all of Schwab's novels – an imaginative, surprisingly moving urban fantasy which builds on the concept of the dead, their histories, and their memories being shelved in an archive. </strong>Schwab has quickly become one of my auto-buy authors. And save for <em>This Savage Song</em>, which was a little out of her familiar comfort zone, her works have never failed to impress me.<br><br>I sensed that Mackenzie Bishop was going to make a relatable heroine from the very first page. There is something to the life Schwab has given this character which I cannot quite name. <strong>Mackenzie grew on me instantly with her slightly rebellious nature, her secrecy, and the weight of her responsibilites and loss on her shoulders.</strong> Perhaps I read this story at an opportune moment, but I was completely open to Mackenzie's grief over her deceased sibling, only to be left raw by it. I almost had to put the book down because it <em>felt</em> so real. <strong>The flashbacks written in 2nd person POV gave her character the depth and background I want in a main character.</strong> It became apparent that her relationship with her grandfather was something precious and pure, and even though I am not a fan of 2nd person POV, it really worked its magic in the flashbacks. Alienated from reality by her destiny – to become a Keeper of the Archive and hunt down escaped Histories (the dead) – Mackenzie wraps an intense loneliness around her. Until she meets Wesley Ayers, that is. What a dreamboat. Mysterious Wesley steps into Mackenzie's world and turns it upside down. <strong>There is no immediate romantic connection, as insta is not how Schwab likes her coffee brewed, but a steady development instead.</strong> The romantic subplot is kept subtle at all times, never overpowering the main plot, which is a specialty of Schwab's books. <strong>Wesley had the necessary amount of self-confidence, cockiness, and snark for a male lead.</strong> I do think that his character could've been more explored, because it felt as though Schwab had only just begun to scrape at his surface. For example, there were only hints at his familial background, and I wanted to see more.<br><br>To be honest, it took me a while to get sucked into the story, which is unusual for me. For the first quarter, it was easy to put <em>The Archived</em> aside. The main plot started to captivate me as soon as something went awry at the Archive. When I smell conspiracies, I'm all in. There is a steady increase of tension as Mackenzie looks for answers. <strong>Though the pacing is on the slow side, the need to get those answers kept me hooked.</strong> As for the romance, I think it was integrated well into the main plot. <strong>I must confess that this is the closest I've ever seen Schwab come to a love triangle but even that aspect fits well into the story.</strong><br><br>There's a reason Schwab has made it onto my auto-buy list, and one of them is her world-building, which has never disappointed me. Compared to other authors which stomp cardboard worlds with no substance out of thin air, it is palpable how much thought and effort Schwab pours into her worlds. <strong>Her world-building – a library for the dead, a place surrounded by the Narrows like a city by suburbs, connected to the outside world through mysterious doors – is nothing short of creative and unique.</strong> Though not necessarily more complex, it took me longer to grasp the concept of this world than, for example, that of <em>A Darker Shade of Magic</em>. For some reason, I experience more difficulties with urban fantasy because the lines between fantasy and reality blur, and it was no different with <em>The Archived</em>. Perhaps it didn't have that much to do with how Schwab created her world, but more with the genre itself.<br><br><strong>Schwab's writing is outstanding in its balance between concise wording and elegant prose.</strong> She wields her words like a painter would a brush, and it's simply the most delicate, elegant written art to behold. Schwab has continuously managed to write beautifully without falling into the trap of purple prose, which is makes her a mastermind of literature, if you ask me. Don't mind me, I'll just keep gushing while you move on to the conclusion of this review.<br><br><strong>As with Schwab's other works, her recipe for <em>The Archived</em> was to create relatable characters, unique world-building, and a subtle romance, underpinned by her most beautiful and skilled writing. Even against her more popular books like <em>Vicious</em> or <em>A Darker Shade of Magic</em>,<em> The Archived</em> can certainly hold its on, and if you've neglected picking this one up, like I have, then I'd say this book's more than deserving of a chance to woo you. </strong></span>
  <a data-text-id="15865475012560810535" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1863076850" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7006404917781467019"><br/><i> Buddy read #1 with my favourite yam ever, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/29249069-pragya' rel='nofollow noopener'>Yammy aka Pragya</a> </i><br/><br/><br/><b> <i> This masterpiece has got to be my all-time favourite Victoria Schwab book. *_* </i> </b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483579876i/21627318._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>It’s mystic, it’s creepy, it’s daunting, it’s absolutely brilliant!!<br/><br/><i> The Archived </i> delves into the unknown world. Mackenzie Bishop has been a Keep for four years, stopping unfortunate Histories when the awake and guiding them back into the Archive. But her job is a secret, one that she must hide from the ones she loves with constant lies. <br/><br/>When Mackenzie’s </span>
  <span id="freeText7006404917781467019" style="display:none"><br><i> Buddy read #1 with my favourite yam ever, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/29249069-pragya" rel="nofollow noopener">Yammy aka Pragya</a> </i><br><br><br><b> <i> This masterpiece has got to be my all-time favourite Victoria Schwab book. *_* </i> </b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483579876i/21627318._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It’s mystic, it’s creepy, it’s daunting, it’s absolutely brilliant!!<br><br><i> The Archived </i> delves into the unknown world. Mackenzie Bishop has been a Keep for four years, stopping unfortunate Histories when the awake and guiding them back into the Archive. But her job is a secret, one that she must hide from the ones she loves with constant lies. <br><br>When Mackenzie’s family moves away to escape their gloomy past, Mackenzie begins to question all that her grandfather has taught her which leads her to notice a mysterious change overtaking the Achieve.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483579876i/21627319.jpg" width="400" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Schwab has strung an incredible tale, nothing like her other work, and I’m ashamed to say I haven’t read it earlier. The writing is so mysteriously poetic and really sets you into the setting. (I’ll admit there were times when I was a little creeped out – okay, a lot!)<br><br>She manages too knit a mystery in-between the chapters that has our minds spinning for the solution!<br><br>The characters are so strong and unique, harboring their secrets while they try to live what resembles a normal life. They are witty and sweet and pretty darn adorable. <br><br>If you can’t already tell, my heart is sold on <i> Wesley Ayers. </i> <s> and it’s not <b> just </b> because he wears eyeliner, sheesh </s><br><br>And Roland, oh my gosh, that precious librarian!!! Someone keep supplying him with <i> red chucks </i> and <i> trashy magazines, </i> plz and thank you. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483579876i/21627320.jpg" width="400" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There’s something so captivating about the book, honestly you <b> need </b> to pick it up right now!!<br><br><br><i> "Stay alive long enough to mess up again. </i><br><br><br>4.5 stars!!<br></span>

<div id="review_2222012103" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2222012103" />
    <a title="Faith M ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29390149-faith-m"><img alt="Faith M ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587515873p2/29390149.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2222012103?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Faith M ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Faith M ✨" href="/user/show/29390149-faith-m">Faith M ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=underrated-gems">underrated-gems</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=need-to-own">need-to-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=1st-person">1st-person</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=mc-gurl">mc-gurl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=read-2018">read-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2222012103" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12965997342318559121">!!!!!<br/><br/><blockquote>I suppose it doesn't matter how they get out. All that matters is they do. And when they do, they must be found. They must go back.</blockquote><br/><b>
  <u>The Writing and the Worldbuilding</u>
</b><br/><br/>So I'm low-key freaking out a little because my current WIP has some parallels to this (afterlife, dead younger brother the female Mc wants to bring back to life somehow, and mystical access to memories through touch) and I know I can never top the Schwab, so wish me luck 🤞<br/><br/>The first few chapters of this really didn't do it fo</span>
  <span id="freeText12965997342318559121" style="display:none">!!!!!<br><br><blockquote>I suppose it doesn't matter how they get out. All that matters is they do. And when they do, they must be found. They must go back.</blockquote><br><b>
  <u>The Writing and the Worldbuilding</u>
</b><br><br>So I'm low-key freaking out a little because my current WIP has some parallels to this (afterlife, dead younger brother the female Mc wants to bring back to life somehow, and mystical access to memories through touch) and I know I can never top the Schwab, so wish me luck 🤞<br><br>The first few chapters of this really didn't do it for me, I must admit. They were slow and, frankly, a little boring, and I really didn't like the narration style very much at first. BUT! Once it grew on me, I ADORED EVERYTHING!!<br><br>It really kinda gave me <i>Cruel Beauty</i> vibes with a specific ghostly character and also some The Mortal Instruments vibes as well. I could almost taste the shapes of what would become her later books, like <i>A Darker Shade of Magic</i> and <i>This Savage Song</i>. The framework is all there and it's kinda amazing to see the earlier incarnations of what is kinda becoming Schwab's main theme.<br><br>The world is AWESOME! I love afterlife stories with a passion (like my doomed WIP). The characters and themes are so multidimensional! The mystery was masterful.<br><br>Me at the end:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1543723293i/26676377._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I still have some holds barred on why those exposition-in-the-past sections were addressed to her grandfather, but maybe the sequel will shed some light. I liked them but didn't see the narrative significance.<br><br><blockquote>Truths are messy and lies are messy, and I don’t care what Da said, it’s impossible to cut a person into pielike pieces, neat and tidy.</blockquote><br><b>
  <u>The Characters</u>
</b><br><br><b>Mac:</b> She's tough and sad and basically pretty great. Sometimes her constant evasion got on my nerves, but it was well characterized so it didn't bother me on a literary level. I really loved her arc.<br><br><b>Guyliner:</b> He's the 2013 punk dream boat and honestly, I love him. He's so funny and his banter with Mackenzie really did it for me.<br><br><b>Owen:</b> HANDS DOWN MY FAV LIKE OH MY GOSH SPENCER REID DID NOT SEE IT COMING<br><br>The other characters were all equally well developed and realistic. The Librarians were definitely the least developed for all the time we see them in the story, but I expect to go deeper in the next book.<br><br><blockquote>I want the things most people don’t notice. The ring and the key and the way you have of wearing everything on the inside.</blockquote><br><b>
  <u>Conclusion</u>
</b><br><br>I want a TV show pronto.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12965997342318559121" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer15198233903231138456">It’s confusing, it’s heartstopping. <b>And it’s so unbelieveably <i>Schwab</i>, if you know what I mean. <br/></b><br/><blockquote>
  <i>We are nothing but recorded moments.</i>
</blockquote><br/>There’s a reason I’m head over heels in love with her. The closest any author has come to this feeling <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1330292.Maggie_Stiefvater' title='Maggie Stiefvater' rel='nofollow noopener'>Maggie Stiefvater</a>, and while I’m more than happy to sell my firstborn for her, she just doesn’t have the magic <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3099544.Victoria_Schwab' title='Victoria Schwab' rel='nofollow noopener'>Victoria Schwab</a> does. <br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i><b>What if</b> echoes through my head as I hunt.<br/><b>What if</b> haunts me through the Narrows.<br/><b>What if</b> follows me home.</i>

  <span id="freeText15198233903231138456" style="display:none">It’s confusing, it’s heartstopping. <b>And it’s so unbelieveably <i>Schwab</i>, if you know what I mean. <br></b><br><blockquote>
  <i>We are nothing but recorded moments.</i>
</blockquote><br>There’s a reason I’m head over heels in love with her. The closest any author has come to this feeling <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1330292.Maggie_Stiefvater" title="Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">Maggie Stiefvater</a>, and while I’m more than happy to sell my firstborn for her, she just doesn’t have the magic <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3099544.Victoria_Schwab" title="Victoria Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">Victoria Schwab</a> does. <br><br><blockquote>

I certainly don’t have anything against Wesley Ayers (look, I'm as much in love with him as the next person) <i>but</i>, he’s no reason to read this book. <br><b><br>Mackenzie Bishop is. <br>The crazy to the point of endearing word building is. <br>The freakish plot is. <br>Victoria Schwab’s awe-inspiring writing style is.<br></b><br>It’s been so long since I devoured a book in one sitting, and am I glad this was the book. From chapter one, I was hooked to the core. This isn’t all <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13638125-vicious" rel="nofollow noopener">crazy anti heroes and mindgames</a>, but it isn’t <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20764879-a-gathering-of-shadows" rel="nofollow noopener">backstabbing and pirates and kisses</a> either. <i>It’s different. </i><br><blockquote>

</blockquote><br><b>But hey, it’s a well known fact I’m Schwab trash.   <i>I never stop wondering about the who and the why. I just learn to stop admitting it.</i>

<div id="review_1209544714" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1209544714?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anja H." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anja H." href="/user/show/6054186-anja-h">Anja H.</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1209544714" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13203955400347942485"><b>*4 KEEPER STARS*</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>“Because the only way to truly record a person is not in words, not in still frames, but in bone and skin and memory.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>All hail Victoria Schwab and her active imagination!<br/>This was another exciting and unique adventure and I can't wait to read more!</span>
