<div id="review_518346478" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/518346478" />
    <a title="Merna " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16392157-merna"><img alt="Merna " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1358143553p2/16392157.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/518346478?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Merna " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Merna " href="/user/show/16392157-merna">Merna </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16392157-merna?shelf=my-2013-reads">my-2013-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16392157-merna?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16392157-merna?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16392157-merna?shelf=uninteresting-characters">uninteresting-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16392157-merna?shelf=could-have-been-good">could-have-been-good</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer518346478" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4155791411539868061"><b>Actual rating:</b> 2.5 stars <br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>Imagine a place where the dead rest on shelves like books.Each body has a story to tell, a life seen in pictures that only Librarians can read. The dead are called Histories, and the vast realm in which they rest is the Archive.</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><b>Initial reaction when reading the blurb: </b> Yeah, I sooo want to read this! <br/><br/><b>Reaction after finishing: </b> meh...<br/><br/>Blurbs are one of the utmost misleading information to be given to a reader. Reading a blurb and thinking it sounds decent is like watch</span>
  <span id="freeText4155791411539868061" style="display:none"><b>Actual rating:</b> 2.5 stars <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Imagine a place where the dead rest on shelves like books.Each body has a story to tell, a life seen in pictures that only Librarians can read. The dead are called Histories, and the vast realm in which they rest is the Archive.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>Initial reaction when reading the blurb: </b> Yeah, I sooo want to read this! <br /><br /><b>Reaction after finishing: </b> meh...<br /><br />Blurbs are one of the utmost misleading information to be given to a reader. Reading a blurb and thinking it sounds decent is like watching a movie trailer, and thinking the film itself is awesome, primarily based on all the cool visual effects shown. <br /><br />From the rating - it seems as if I enjoyed the Archived. It was entertaining from time to time. The writing was also decent. But as I kept reading along, I realized the archive (the main storyline of the whole book) is strikingly stupid. <br /><br />This book wanted to be original. <br /><br />This book wanted to be unique.<br /><br /><b>But it simply wasn’t.</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“I didn’t want to accept it, but the fact is, they were people. Copies of people. Because the only way to truly record a person is not in words, not in still frames, but in bone and skin and memory.”</i>
</blockquote> <br /><br />Sounds all clever and new in the science-fiction/fantasy genre, doesn’t it? But several people who will read this book will skip one simple thing. The Actual point behind the Archive. So, in basic term you’ve got copies of these dead people stacked in a place called the Archive which is organized by the librarians, who are the only ones able to access it. But what’s the point, if the only people able to enter the Archives are the librarians? Why bother making copies of millions of dead people, if in the end there’s nothing beneficial or effective about this entire system? You can almost imagine my absolute confusion when someone attempted to bring this utterly useless system down. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“I want freedom,” he says, stalking me. “The Archive is a prison, and not only for the dead. And that’s why I’m going to tear it down, shelf by shelf and branch by branch.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Even with an explanation, I was still unable to comprehend the reason behind bringing down the Archive. <br /><br />It’s almost as if the author had this amazing idea and was completely excited by it, that she rapidly started writing the book before she even began to structure it thoroughly. I’m not sure if I even want to get into the mystery part of this book. Mystery can be thought-provoking with very skilful writers. Most of the writers that are capable of constructing a beautiful mystery have an understanding in criminology. I’m not convinced this author did. In most of the books the person who turns out to be the psychotic antagonist is the person you least suspect, who you actually end up suspecting nonetheless. Yet, the authors are still are unaware of this. <br /><br />The heroine Mackenzie Bishop is a keeper. She guards the place known as the narrows. It’s a place where histories (dead copy of people) go when they escape the Archive, and her duty is to catch them swiftly and put them back into the Archive before they escape into the real world. Woah! The Heroine’s role sounds interesting. Though, it wasn’t. All Mackenzie did was catch dead people and put them into the Archive. That’s all she did. At first it was cool then it wasn’t. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>With Wesley, there is too much to lose. But with Owen, there is no future to be lost by giving in. No future at all. Only escape. </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Yes, it’s time for the romance part of the book.<br /><br />As we have observed from the quote above there's a love triangle. Two love interests. <br /><br /><b>One who:</b><br />Wore eyeliner and never stopped complimenting himself on how handsomely attractive he was. <br /><br /><b>And the other:</b><br />Well, umm he was dead. <br /><br />I wasn’t a fan of the romance. It was just a big capitalized NO for me. Actually, I disliked the romance because it was awfully monotonous. <br /><br /><b>I noticed something else as I went through this book and I will make it as explanatory as possible.</b> <br /><br />All of us probably watch sitcom shows, right? Shows such as big bang theory or how I met your mother. A big major detail we pick up on is the setting. The settings in sitcom shows are always the same, virtually in every episode. For example every episodes of how I met your mother will be held in apartment or a bar – not always but regularly. <br /><br />The setting in the book for the archived is in Coronado which is located in San Diego, but I’m pretty sure the author never stated that, however that’s not the problem. The problem is the author doesn’t use the Coronado setting to her advantage. Throughout the entire novel the only place I’ve gotten a description of is the narrows or the apartment. I felt so trapped. The narrator never goes anywhere besides those two main places. I truly don’t see how someone cannot view this as irritating. <br /><br />It all seems strange because I still granted the book almost three stars. I only did this because of the potential – there was so much potential. <br /><br />I have too many things to say about this book, but I won’t be able to voice them all because they’re all entwined to make these conflicting emotions, which I can’t put into words since they won’t make any sense to others. <br /><br /><b>Maybe you should give the book a shot/maybe you shouldn’t.</b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4155791411539868061" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1018786181" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1018786181" />
    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1018786181?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=likeable-mc">likeable-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=pnr-uf">pnr-uf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=made-me-laugh">made-me-laugh</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1018786181" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5676330081430572105">❤ <b>Buddy read with the wonderful <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1088309053' rel='nofollow noopener'>Chelsea</a></b>❤<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1417893676i/12591578._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>" What if I mess up? "<br/>" Oh, you will. You’ll mess up, you’ll make mistakes, you’ll break things. Some you’ll be able to piece together, and others you’ll lose. That’s all a given. But there’s only one thing you have to do for me. "<br/>" What’s that? "<br/>" Stay alive enough to mess up again. "</b><br/><br/> <u>See, I don't know if that's because</u> : <br/><br/><i>a)</i> I actually read a lot of <i>slow-paced-kill-me-now</i> books when I was in college - like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/210255.Against_Nature' rel='nofollow noopener'>this one</a>, the <i>riveting</i> story of a man who decides</span>
  <span id="freeText5676330081430572105" style="display:none">❤ <b>Buddy read with the wonderful <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1088309053" rel="nofollow noopener">Chelsea</a></b>❤<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1417893676i/12591578._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>" What if I mess up? "<br>" Oh, you will. You’ll mess up, you’ll make mistakes, you’ll break things. Some you’ll be able to piece together, and others you’ll lose. That’s all a given. But there’s only one thing you have to do for me. "<br>" What’s that? "<br>" Stay alive enough to mess up again. "</b><br><br> <u>See, I don't know if that's because</u> : <br><br><i>a)</i> I actually read a lot of <i>slow-paced-kill-me-now</i> books when I was in college - like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/210255.Against_Nature" rel="nofollow noopener">this one</a>, the <i>riveting</i> story of a man who decides to never go out of his house anymore <i>because "too much luxury, people!"</i> and intends to describe everything he thinks or sees or does in his freakin house during about 3 months (yes, that's as horrible as it sounds and yes, I had to read it like, 3 times. My eyes are still hurting - and I don't care how <i>mind-blowing</i> it's supposed to be - I read French literature <b>so. damn. better.</b>)<br><br><i>b)</i> I used to be a fantasy fan, <i>aka</i> a reader who used to go through 3 books in a series before - <br>✶ getting in the middle of the action, <br>✶ understand who is Tennahra and Kileken exactly (yes, I'm typing randomly on my keypad) and why the King/the Queen/The Witch/*add random character here* are such weirdoes. <br><br>But what do I know? <b>In my opinion the beginning isn't dull or boring. It's called... <i>watch out, big big words!</i> world-building people. Characterization.</b><br><br>I know, that's pretty rare out there. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1417893676i/12591579._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b><u>Striking fact# 1</u> : The writing was impressive</b><br><br>The story is told from two different times : in present day, we follow Mackenzie, the youngest <i>Keeper</i> in the <i>Archive</i> organization (whose purpose is to keep the dead quiet on shelves), when her family moves in the Coronado Hotel whereas other parts let us have a glimpse of the memories of her training which took place years before - before her grandpa died. <br><br><b>Before her baby brother died, jeopardizing all her family, leaving an incurable wound in their heart.</b> <br><br><b>I loved the writing, which contains the kind of magical blissfulness</b> I found in <i>The Raven Boys</i> - we're struck by the way the objects seem to be brought to life somehow. The only thing we have to do is to let ourselves get lost in these corridors, walking through these doors hidden behind our consciousness, and enjoy the enchanted feeling created by Victoria Schwab's pen. <br><br> I ruined my post-it reserve I had created for... work. Bad me. <br> <br><b>" Why? "<br>You take the cigarette out, jabbing the air with the unlit tip. "That is the most worthless question in the world. Use your words. Be specific. <i>Why</i> is like <i>bah</i> or <i>moo</i> or that silly sound pigeons make."</b><br><br><b><u>Striking fact# 2</u> : The story fascinated <i>and</i> enthralled me from the beginning to the end : I was hooked.</b> <br><br>I won't get back to the <i>no, I don't think the beginning is boring</i> conversation, because hey, I'm pretty sure you saw my point earlier. <br><br>So let's go straight, shall we? <br><br>- The <b>world-building</b> is <b>inventive</b> and filled with <b>originality</b>. Of course it is! Seriously, have you ever heard about <i>dead people</i> resting on <i>shelves</i>? <i>Keepers</i> whose job consists of hunting <i>Histories</i>, <i>aka</i> dead who're not so comfortable on their shelves? Well?<br><br>- Now, the <b>romance</b>. You're worried to find another love at first sight/love overtakes the plot/whatever love does? <br><b><u>Try this</u> : friendship, getting to know each other, light and smile-inducing flirting.</b> <br><br>- Here's a mystery book which actually contains a <b>mystery</b>. I know. I'm excited too. <i>That</i> plot? <b>Thrilling. Intoxicating.</b> Slightly creepy at times. Because <b>murderer people! Trust issues! Bunch of lies!</b> <br><br><i>Oh. My. Am I bad to love that so damn much?</i><br><br>- Also, <i>Histories' waking up</i>? It gets a strong but awesome zombie vibe, without the lame heroine - yes, you got me! I don't like zombie books! While here I found it fascinating.<br><br><b><u>Striking fact# 3</u> : Can I have more of these characters, pretty please?</b> <br><br>As I said earlier, I was amazed by the characterization qualities : you won't believe me, but we <b>get the impression to really <i>know</i> the characters</b>, who are far from the ghosts we're sometimes accustomed to. Now tell me, how incredible is that? <br><br><b>"Well, there's this new girl who just moved in on floor three. Her family re-opening the café. I hear she likes to lie, and hit people."<br>"Oh yeah? Well, there's that strange goth guy, the one who's always lurking around Five C."<br>" Strangely hot in a mysterious way, though, right?"</b><br><br><i>Multiple choice quiz time!</i><br><br><b>Mackenzie..…</b> <br>✘<s>can’t stop thinking about the eyes of some boy</s><br>✔ genuinely thinks before acting<br>✘<s> makes me want to throw the book in my chimney with her annoying crappie thoughts</s><br>✔ could be a friend of mine – apart from the fact she can’t really have friends, of course, duh.<br><br><b>"<i>M</i>. That's what I call her, this normal, nonexistent me. (...) I can pretend to be M ; I can wear her like a mask. But I can't <i>be</i> her. I'll never be.<br>M wouldn't see blood-covered boys in her bedroom.<br>M wouldn't spend her time scouring her dead brother's toys for a glimpse of his life."</b><br><br><b>Wes…. </b><br>✘<s> is the savior everybody was waiting for. Hey, what did you expect? He’s a boy dammit!</s><br>✔ likes blueberry cupcakes and ... let's see... Did I smile so big it hurt each time he made an apparition? <b>Absolutely.</b><br>✔ wears guyliner. Okay, I know, nobody cares about that, but - <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1417893676i/12591580.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Riiiiiight?</i><br>✔ is genuinely interested in Mackenzie, takes her feelings in consideration, and never tries to take the decision out of her.<br><br><b>" It's the same for me, you know? This is all new to me. And I'm not going anywhere. It takes at least three assassination attempts to scare me off. And even then, if there are baked goods involved, I might come back. "</b><br><br><b>Roland….</b><br>✔ Is an Archive Librarian whose age isn’t really clear and whose life is a mystery and whose choices are full of selflessness and caring and courage, okay?<br><br><b>Why, thank you, can I have the sequel pretty please?</b><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>

<div id="review_1845720703" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1845720703" />
    <a title="Irene△⃒⃘➰" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55991704-irene"><img alt="Irene△⃒⃘➰" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603216583p2/55991704.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1845720703?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Irene△⃒⃘➰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Irene△⃒⃘➰" href="/user/show/55991704-irene">Irene△⃒⃘➰</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781423171089" href="/book/show/17899647-the-archived">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55991704-irene?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1845720703" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5743801381308286644"><b>3.75/5</b><br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>“Everything is valuable, in its own way. Everything is full of history.”</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>This was a <b>very interesting read.</b><br/>The plot and story is <b>kinda easy to follow</b> (except for some parts toward the end) and at the same time it intrigued me a lot.<br/><br/>I immediately liked that our girl, Mac had to restart her life after moving to a new place, the Coronado, following the death of her brother, Ben. <br/>I have a thing with that concept and <b>I always find very interesting reading and seeing how people live when every</b></span>
  <span id="freeText5743801381308286644" style="display:none"><b>3.75/5</b><br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“Everything is valuable, in its own way. Everything is full of history.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />This was a <b>very interesting read.</b><br />The plot and story is <b>kinda easy to follow</b> (except for some parts toward the end) and at the same time it intrigued me a lot.<br /><br />I immediately liked that our girl, Mac had to restart her life after moving to a new place, the Coronado, following the death of her brother, Ben. <br />I have a thing with that concept and <b>I always find very interesting reading and seeing how people live when everything is different</b>. How they interact with new people and how they deal with their new house.<br />And <b>I loved the idea of the Archived itself</b> and especially what Mac’s purpose is in all of this. There are some flashback too that very very cool to read, we learn a fairly good amount of things of her past and how everything started for her.<br /><br />She finally meets too someone with whom she can about talk about all of this, because Wesley is too a part of this world.<br />Her role here is to find escaped Histories around the Narrows and turn them in, she is a Keeper.<br />She has this little note book like thing, where names are scribbled when she has a new job, and they disappear once completed.<br />Meanwhile she finds that something creepy happened at the Coronado years ago and searching through its history she finds that some records are missing…<br /><br />Said this, <b>there’s a lot going on in this book</b>. Even if everything is pretty simple to understand there are a lot of events and details. <br />I think that <b>this was mainly a mystery</b> but a mystery with a twist.<br />All the Histories' concept is very unique and I liked too how this plot developed. <br /><b>There were some parts of the ending that didn’t fully convince me</b> but overall I never read something like this before and found it very entertaining! </span>
  <a data-text-id="5743801381308286644" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1609087409" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1609087409" />
    <a title="Poonam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17656456-poonam"><img alt="Poonam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520691179p2/17656456.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1609087409?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Poonam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Poonam" href="/user/show/17656456-poonam">Poonam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17656456-poonam?shelf=group-reads">group-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17656456-poonam?shelf=paranormal-or-fantasy">paranormal-or-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17656456-poonam?shelf=ya-na">ya-na</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1609087409" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5539046760054054067"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/><i>This is my Book Of the Month- January 2017, with GR group- Nothing But Reading Challenges- Category: Young Adult BOM.</i><br/><br/>The concept of this book is splendid-- The dead are called Histories, and the vast realm in which they rest is the Archive. Imagine, every live ever lived, all the memories in a library, secured!<br/><b>
  <i>"The Outer, which you don't waste much breath on because it's everything around us, the normal world, the only one most people ever know about. The Narrows, a nightmarish place</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText5539046760054054067" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b><br><br><i>This is my Book Of the Month- January 2017, with GR group- Nothing But Reading Challenges- Category: Young Adult BOM.</i><br><br>The concept of this book is splendid-- The dead are called Histories, and the vast realm in which they rest is the Archive. Imagine, every live ever lived, all the memories in a library, secured!<br><b>
  <i>"The Outer, which you don't waste much breath on because it's everything around us, the normal world, the only one most people ever know about. The Narrows, a nightmarish place, all stained corridors and distant whispers, doors and darkness thick like grime. And the Archive, a library of the dead, vast and warm, wood and stone and colored glass, and all throughout, a sense of peace."</i>
</b><br><br>**Mild Spoilers Ahead**<br><br>Mackenzie Bishop is a Keeper and her job is to ensure that the Histories remain in the Archive and do not escape to the Outer World. This is a huge task for a 16 year old girl to undertake....<br><b>
  <i>"A confession: sometimes I dream of being normal. I dream about this girl who looks like me and talks like me, but isn't me."</i>
</b><br>My problem with this concept was that Mac started as a keeper at the age of 12!! That's right, no kidding! This was a little too much even for a fantasy novel.<br><br>Apart from being the keeper, Mac is also dealing with the loss of her brother's life...<br><b>
  <i>"My brother left a hole, and it's starting to close. And when it does, he'll be gone. Really and truly gone. Isn't this what I wanted? For my parents to stop running? For my family to heal? But what if I'm not ready to let Ben go?"</i>
</b><br>I really like this whole bit in the book as it made Mac seem more real to me.<br><br>There are some interesting characters and few good twists and turns that keep you turning the pages.<br><br>The thing is, I expected this book to be more deep but it is on the side of a fluff YA read. There are some plot points that are open and I guess will be solved in the next book, maybe....<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1473462069ra/20468336.gif" height="" width="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Nevertheless this is a good read and overall I enjoyed the story and how it ended, there sure are some creepy moments in the Narrows!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="5539046760054054067" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1432261836" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1432261836" />
    <a title="Phrynne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8655084-phrynne"><img alt="Phrynne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577753809p2/8655084.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1432261836?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Phrynne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phrynne" href="/user/show/8655084-phrynne">Phrynne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1432261836" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17133905675078691522"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3099544.Victoria_Schwab' title='Victoria Schwab' rel='nofollow noopener'>Victoria Schwab</a> has such a brilliant imagination.I am loving all her books including the ones she writes as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7168230.V_E__Schwab' title='V.E. Schwab' rel='nofollow noopener'>V.E. Schwab</a> In this book we have a library of the dead, literally. Dead bodies storing all their memories and experiences forever. Of course there have to be Librarians to organise the archives and Keepers whose job it is to retrieve the occasional body which happens to "wake up". The story is fun and well paced and the characters are all well written and interesting. I thoroughly enjoyed </span>
  <span id="freeText17133905675078691522" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3099544.Victoria_Schwab" title="Victoria Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">Victoria Schwab</a> has such a brilliant imagination.I am loving all her books including the ones she writes as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7168230.V_E__Schwab" title="V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">V.E. Schwab</a> In this book we have a library of the dead, literally. Dead bodies storing all their memories and experiences forever. Of course there have to be Librarians to organise the archives and Keepers whose job it is to retrieve the occasional body which happens to "wake up". The story is fun and well paced and the characters are all well written and interesting. I thoroughly enjoyed it and am looking forward to the sequel. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17133905675078691522" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ln6ijUS4f3vKOl1OKDr7cRVB2EGf9VK5zbCDTLDt1BGsWMtf/+a2E20R6S/fz/Guwx4/iVF43N6WzsX9fa4miw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pVR9KbWZ29fpb1cH57NlIpSuLqyoT4bFzZrgzNhbfhOfchT7DscSv05E42YQRm/9QvHJZGbCCKKW5KZ9FRiMiQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer14800470512153358872">Victoria is the product of a British mother, a Beverly Hills father, and a southern upbringing. Because of this, she has been known to say "tom-ah-toes," "like," and "y'all."<br/><br/>She also tells stories.<br/><br/>She loves fairy tales, and folklore, and stories that make her wonder if the world is really as it seems. <br/></span>
